        }

          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }
        .container-issue-content {
          padding: 0;
          flex-grow: 1;
          display: flex;

          box-sizing: border-box;
          padding-top: 0.5em;
        }

          box-sizing: border-box;
          width: 100%;
          max-width: 100%;
          margin: auto;
          padding: 0;
          display: flex;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: space-between;
          flex-direction: row;
          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }
        .container-no-issue {
          padding: 0.5em 16px;
          font-size: var(--chops-large-font-size);
        }

          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);

          border-right: var(--chops-normal-border);

          width: 24em;
          min-width: 256px;
          flex-grow: 0;
          flex-shrink: 0;
          box-sizing: border-box;
          z-index: 100;
        }
        .issue-header-container {
          z-index: 10;
          position: sticky;
          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          margin-bottom: 0.25em;
          width: 100%;
        }
        mr-issue-details {
          min-width: 50%;
          max-width: 1000px;
          flex-grow: 1;
          box-sizing: border-box;
          min-height: 100%;

          padding-right: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);
        }
        mr-issue-metadata {
          position: sticky;
          overflow-y: auto;
          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }
        mr-launch-overview {
          border-left: var(--chops-normal-border);

            flex-direction: column;

          }
          mr-issue-details, mr-launch-overview {
            width: 100%;

          }
        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

We operate under the assumption that there is always a tab in the tab group. when deleting tab groups we delete the group and then delete the tabs in order to keep the assumption. Removing this assumption in ListTabs could cause a lot of other bugs, so its important to understand why we are getting into the state where there's no tab in the tab group in the first place.



<span class="line"><!---->We operate under the assumption that there is always a tab in the tab group. when deleting tab groups we delete the group and then delete the tabs in order to keep the assumption. Removing this assumption in ListTabs could cause a lot of other bugs, so its important to understand why we are getting into the state where there's no tab in the tab group in the first place.<!----></span>

I agree with David that we should not allow empty tab groups to exist. We could:



<span class="line"><!---->I agree with David that we should not allow empty tab groups to exist. We could:<!----></span>



<br>





1. change ListTabs to CHECK that there's a last tab, so at least this isn't a security issue,



<span class="line"><!---->1. change ListTabs to CHECK that there's a last tab, so at least this isn't a security issue,<!----></span>



<br>





2. go through the webui tabstrip's use of the tab groups API to figure out how it's putting the model into an invalid state,



<span class="line"><!---->2. go through the webui tabstrip's use of the tab groups API to figure out how it's putting the model into an invalid state,<!----></span>



<br>





3. add a (D)CHECK to the model when it's asked to enter an invalid state, or by some other, gentler means make it impossible to actually get into an invalid state even if our callers ask us nicely to do so.



<span class="line"><!---->3. add a (D)CHECK to the model when it's asked to enter an invalid state, or by some other, gentler means make it impossible to actually get into an invalid state even if our callers ask us nicely to do so.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





IMO we should do 2 and 3. Landing 3 will fix the security issue (and prevent future ones), and landing 2 will stop the crashing that might be happening instead.



<span class="line"><!---->IMO we should do 2 and 3. Landing 3 will fix the security issue (and prevent future ones), and landing 2 will stop the crashing that might be happening instead.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'll work on 3 and hand back to tluk@ for #2 once that's far enough along to be helpful.



<span class="line"><!---->I'll work on 3 and hand back to tluk@ for #2 once that's far enough along to be helpful.<!----></span>

Okay starting to execute on that plan and realizing we've got this all wrong. A few corrections to comments from above:



<span class="line"><!---->Okay starting to execute on that plan and realizing we've got this all wrong. A few corrections to comments from above:<!----></span>



<br>





#3, #15: the GetLastTab thing is a red herring. GetLastTab not being nullopt is definitely a safe assumption, because GetFirstTab was not nullopt and these can only be nullopt if the group is empty, therefore they will always be nullopt together.



<span class="line"><!---->#3, #15: the GetLastTab thing is a red herring. GetLastTab not being nullopt is definitely a safe assumption, because GetFirstTab was not nullopt and these can only be nullopt if the group is empty, therefore they will always be nullopt together.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





#17, #19: Looks like we can in fact tolerate empty groups, or at least ListTabs itself is fine with them. That's not what's happening here.



<span class="line"><!---->#17, #19: Looks like we can in fact tolerate empty groups, or at least ListTabs itself is fine with them. That's not what's happening here.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Instead it looks like the failure is the DCHECK just below firing when it detects a discontiguous group - i.e. a tab group split in two by a tab not in the group.  That is a situation that can lead to explosions (including security-relevant ones), but the TabStripModel/TabGroupModel APIs do allow entering that state. To some extent that's necessary, because we implement some multi-step operations* in such a way that the group is split transiently but contiguous after the full operation is complete.



<span class="line"><!---->Instead it looks like the failure is the DCHECK just below firing when it detects a discontiguous group - i.e. a tab group split in two by a tab not in the group.  That is a situation that can lead to explosions (including security-relevant ones), but the TabStripModel/TabGroupModel APIs do allow entering that state. To some extent that's necessary, because we implement some multi-step operations* in such a way that the group is split transiently but contiguous after the full operation is complete.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It looks to me like the tab dragging session on the webui side is being interrupted by the extension's actions, and invalidating some assumptions that the webui drag session is making when it performs its own multi-step operations. A lot of similar things have happened on the Views side, and we've added numerous mitigations to avoid these kinds of issues, notably including:



<span class="line"><!---->It looks to me like the tab dragging session on the webui side is being interrupted by the extension's actions, and invalidating some assumptions that the webui drag session is making when it performs its own multi-step operations. A lot of similar things have happened on the Views side, and we've added numerous mitigations to avoid these kinds of issues, notably including:<!----></span>



<br>





- When a tab was just opened while we're dragging a window in a tab drag session, complete the current drag session (unless the drag session itself did the opening).



<span class="line"><!---->- When a tab was just opened while we're dragging a window in a tab drag session, complete the current drag session (unless the drag session itself did the opening).<!----></span>



<br>





- When a tab that's being dragged is about to be closed, complete the current drag session (unless the drag session itself is doing the closing).



<span class="line"><!---->- When a tab that's being dragged is about to be closed, complete the current drag session (unless the drag session itself is doing the closing).<!----></span>



<br>





- Prevent extensions from calling mutating APIs during a tab drag session (note that this does not cover pages opening/closing themselves, hence the first two mitigations). We added the IsTabStripEditable signal path for this, which allows the tabs and sessions APIs to check with the TabStrip view and maybe block extension calls.



<span class="line"><!---->- Prevent extensions from calling mutating APIs during a tab drag session (note that this does not cover pages opening/closing themselves, hence the first two mitigations). We added the IsTabStripEditable signal path for this, which allows the tabs and sessions APIs to check with the TabStrip view and maybe block extension calls.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So, options redux:



<span class="line"><!---->So, options redux:<!----></span>



<br>





A. Make it impossible to enter those states via TSM/TGM APIs. Very big refactor, dpenning@ is working on stuff in that space, it's not tractable for a security bug fix.



<span class="line"><!---->A. Make it impossible to enter those states via TSM/TGM APIs. Very big refactor, dpenning@ is working on stuff in that space, it's not tractable for a security bug fix.<!----></span>



<br>





B. Have Webui tabstrip adopt mitigations like the Views side has to avoid this kind of concurrent modification situation. I don't know exactly what might need to be done here, as I'm not familiar with what assumptions the webui dragging code is making re: things changing out from under it.



<span class="line"><!---->B. Have Webui tabstrip adopt mitigations like the Views side has to avoid this kind of concurrent modification situation. I don't know exactly what might need to be done here, as I'm not familiar with what assumptions the webui dragging code is making re: things changing out from under it.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Handing it back to webui folks so they can do option B.  Happy to support you if you need help with this!



<span class="line"><!---->Handing it back to webui folks so they can do option B.  Happy to support you if you need help with this!<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>



<br>



<br>





*: For example - pinning a tab that's in the middle of a group must remove it from the group and move it to the start of the tabstrip, but neither of those operations can be done first without splitting the tab group. We'd have to either do both of those simultaneously (i.e. bundle the notifications together, which our observer API doesn't support) or first move the tab to the edge of the group, ungroup it, and then move it to its final destination, which generates spurious observer notifications that don't map intuitively to the user's actions.



<span class="line"><!---->*: For example - pinning a tab that's in the middle of a group must remove it from the group and move it to the start of the tabstrip, but neither of those operations can be done first without splitting the tab group. We'd have to either do both of those simultaneously (i.e. bundle the notifications together, which our observer API doesn't support) or first move the tab to the edge of the group, ungroup it, and then move it to its final destination, which generates spurious observer notifications that don't map intuitively to the user's actions.<!----></span>

[webui tab strip] Address crash caused by discontinuous tab group



<span class="line"><!---->[webui tab strip] Address crash caused by discontinuous tab group<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL fixes a crash in the WebUI Tab Strip where code in



<span class="line"><!---->This CL fixes a crash in the WebUI Tab Strip where code in<!----></span>



<br>





OnTabStripModelChanged() was testing whether a tab kMoved event



<span class="line"><!---->OnTabStripModelChanged() was testing whether a tab kMoved event<!----></span>



<br>





was the result of a full tab-group move in the tab strip.



<span class="line"><!---->was the result of a full tab-group move in the tab strip.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This was originally done to help optimize the number of IPC calls



<span class="line"><!---->This was originally done to help optimize the number of IPC calls<!----></span>



<br>





made to the tab strip. However a tab kMoved event may leave a tab



<span class="line"><!---->made to the tab strip. However a tab kMoved event may leave a tab<!----></span>



<br>





group in a temporarily dicontinuous state while the event is



<span class="line"><!---->group in a temporarily dicontinuous state while the event is<!----></span>



<br>





propagated in TabStripModelObserver::OnTabStripModelChanged().



<span class="line"><!---->propagated in TabStripModelObserver::OnTabStripModelChanged().<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL removes this optimization and instead propagates the



<span class="line"><!---->This CL removes this optimization and instead propagates the<!----></span>



<br>





individual tab kMoved events to the WebUI in the renderer



<span class="line"><!---->individual tab kMoved events to the WebUI in the renderer<!----></span>



<br>





for processing. This avoids the code needing to check for



<span class="line"><!---->for processing. This avoids the code needing to check for<!----></span>



<br>





tab group contiguity and prevents the crash.



<span class="line"><!---->tab group contiguity and prevents the crash.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Follow up CLs can address improvements in IPC to the renderer.



<span class="line"><!---->Follow up CLs can address improvements in IPC to the renderer.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

[webui tab strip] Add multi-tab group move behavior test



<span class="line"><!---->[webui tab strip] Add multi-tab group move behavior test<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL adds a test that ensures the tab list correctly handles a



<span class="line"><!---->This CL adds a test that ensures the tab list correctly handles a<!----></span>



<br>





multi-tab group move event.



<span class="line"><!---->multi-tab group move event.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is a complex interaction that involves the following series of



<span class="line"><!---->This is a complex interaction that involves the following series of<!----></span>



<br>





events:



<span class="line"><!---->events:<!----></span>



<br>





  1. When moving a group within the tab strip the drag manager will



<span class="line"><!---->  1. When moving a group within the tab strip the drag manager will<!----></span>



<br>





     add the tab group element to the DOM at the appropriate drop



<span class="line"><!---->     add the tab group element to the DOM at the appropriate drop<!----></span>



<br>





     index throughout the course of the drag and drop session.



<span class="line"><!---->     index throughout the course of the drag and drop session.<!----></span>



<br>





  2. When the drag and drop session ends with a successful tab group



<span class="line"><!---->  2. When the drag and drop session ends with a successful tab group<!----></span>



<br>





     move, individual tabMoved() events are generated for each tab in



<span class="line"><!---->     move, individual tabMoved() events are generated for each tab in<!----></span>



<br>





     the group followed by a final tabGroupMoved().



<span class="line"><!---->     the group followed by a final tabGroupMoved().<!----></span>



<br>

The crash itself was a DCHECK crash that was only encountered on debug builds. The DCHECK was tripped when the tab strip was queried while in an inconsistent state - however this does not occur in release builds. The tab strip query was only used to save a few IPCs to the renderer process but was not necessary for correctness (this was removed in the CL above). When this DCHECK is tripped the optimization is not applied however the tab strip's behavior is still WAI.



<span class="line"><!---->The crash itself was a DCHECK crash that was only encountered on debug builds. The DCHECK was tripped when the tab strip was queried while in an inconsistent state - however this does not occur in release builds. The tab strip query was only used to save a few IPCs to the renderer process but was not necessary for correctness (this was removed in the CL above). When this DCHECK is tripped the optimization is not applied however the tab strip's behavior is still WAI.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Given this is a non-issue on release builds I'm inclined to drop the security impact label (feel free to re-add if I'm wrong on my analysis).



<span class="line"><!---->Given this is a non-issue on release builds I'm inclined to drop the security impact label (feel free to re-add if I'm wrong on my analysis).<!----></span>
